Data = read.table(textConnection(Input),header=TRUE)

###  Order factors by the order in data frame
###  Otherwise, R will alphabetize them

Data$treatment = factor(Data$treatment,
                        levels=unique(Data$treatment))

Data$metatranscriptome       = factor(Data$metatranscriptome,
                                      levels=unique(Data$metatranscriptome))

Data$species = factor(Data$species,
                    levels=unique(Data$species))

###  Check the data frame

library(psych)
headTail(Data)
str(Data)
summary(Data)   

### Remove unnecessary objects

rm(Input)


library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)


model = lmer(rank ~ species*treatment + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

summary(model)

###  Order factors by the order in data frame
###  Otherwise, R will alphabetize them

Data$treatment = factor(Data$treatment,
                        levels=unique(Data$treatment))

Data$metatranscriptome       = factor(Data$metatranscriptome,
                                      levels=unique(Data$metatranscriptome))

Data$species = factor(Data$species,
                    levels=unique(Data$species))

###  Check the data frame

library(psych)
headTail(Data)
str(Data)
summary(Data)   

### Remove unnecessary objects

rm(Input)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)


model = lmer(rank ~ species*treatment + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)


Type III Analysis of Variance Table with Satterthwaite's method
                   Sum Sq Mean Sq NumDF  DenDF F value    Pr(>F)    
species             27.64   27.64     1 193.66  0.2641 0.6078701    
treatment          190.26  190.26     1 189.95  1.8185 0.1790946    
species:treatment 1287.67 1287.67     1 189.95 12.3078 0.0005631 ***
---
Signif. codes:  0 ‘***’ 0.001 ‘**’ 0.01 ‘*’ 0.05 ‘.’ 0.1 ‘ ’ 1

###  Order factors by the order in data frame
###  Otherwise, R will alphabetize them

Data$treatment = factor(Data$treatment,
                        levels=unique(Data$treatment))

Data$metatranscriptome       = factor(Data$metatranscriptome,
                                      levels=unique(Data$metatranscriptome))

Data$species = factor(Data$species,
                    levels=unique(Data$species))

###  Check the data frame

library(psych)
headTail(Data)
str(Data)
summary(Data)   

### Remove unnecessary objects

rm(Input)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)


model = lmer(rank ~ species*treatment + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

summary(model)

treatment           3.75    3.75     1   114  0.0782 0.780229   
species:treatment 436.97  436.97     1   114  9.1121 0.003133 **

Data = read.table(textConnection(Input),header=TRUE)

###  Order factors by the order in data frame
###  Otherwise, R will alphabetize them

Data$treatment = factor(Data$treatment,
                        levels=unique(Data$treatment))

Data$metatranscriptome       = factor(Data$metatranscriptome,
                                      levels=unique(Data$metatranscriptome))

Data$species = factor(Data$species,
                    levels=unique(Data$species))

###  Check the data frame

library(psych)
headTail(Data)
str(Data)
summary(Data)   

### Remove unnecessary objects

rm(Input)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)


model = lmer(rank ~ species*treatment + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

summary(model)

Type III Analysis of Variance Table with Satterthwaite's method

treatment           834.2   834.2     1 1545.1  0.1853 0.6669
species:treatment  1192.3  1192.3     1 1545.1  0.2649 0.6068

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)



model = lmer(rank ~ treatment + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)

#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)


model = lmer(rank ~ treatment + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

Data = read.table(textConnection(Input),header=TRUE)

###  Order factors by the order in data frame
###  Otherwise, R will alphabetize them

Data$treatment = factor(Data$treatment,
                        levels=unique(Data$treatment))

Data$metatranscriptome       = factor(Data$metatranscriptome,
                                      levels=unique(Data$metatranscriptome))


###  Check the data frame

library(psych)
headTail(Data)
str(Data)
summary(Data)   

### Remove unnecessary objects

rm(Input)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)



model = lmer(rank ~ treatment + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

summary(model)

Data = read.table(textConnection(Input),header=TRUE)

###  Order factors by the order in data frame
###  Otherwise, R will alphabetize them

Data$treatment = factor(Data$treatment,
                        levels=unique(Data$treatment))

Data$metatranscriptome       = factor(Data$metatranscriptome,
                                      levels=unique(Data$metatranscriptome))


###  Check the data frame

library(psych)
headTail(Data)
str(Data)
summary(Data)   

### Remove unnecessary objects

rm(Input)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)



model = lmer(rank ~ treatment + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

###  Otherwise, R will alphabetize them

                        levels=unique(Data$treatment))

                                      levels=unique(Data$metatranscriptome))

rm(Input)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)



model = lmer(rank ~ treatment + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

                                      levels=unique(Data$metatranscriptome))

### Remove unnecessary objects

rm(Input)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)


model = lmer(rank ~ species + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

summary(model)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)


model = lmer(rank ~ species + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

Data$species = factor(Data$species,
                      levels=unique(Data$species))

Data$metatranscriptome       = factor(Data$metatranscriptome,
                                      levels=unique(Data$metatranscriptome))


###  Check the data frame

library(psych)
headTail(Data)
str(Data)
summary(Data)   

### Remove unnecessary objects

rm(Input)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)


model = lmer(rank ~ species + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

###  Order factors by the order in data frame
###  Otherwise, R will alphabetize them

Data$species = factor(Data$species,
                      levels=unique(Data$species))

                                      levels=unique(Data$metatranscriptome))


###  Check the data frame

library(psych)
headTail(Data)
str(Data)
summary(Data)   

### Remove unnecessary objects

rm(Input)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)


model = lmer(rank ~ species + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)


model = lmer(rank ~ species + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

Data = read.table(textConnection(Input),header=TRUE)

###  Order factors by the order in data frame
###  Otherwise, R will alphabetize them


Data$treatment = factor(Data$treatment,
                        levels=unique(Data$treatment))

Data$metatranscriptome       = factor(Data$metatranscriptome,
                                      levels=unique(Data$metatranscriptome))

Data$species = factor(Data$species,
                    levels=unique(Data$species))

###  Check the data frame

library(psych)
headTail(Data)
str(Data)
summary(Data)   

### Remove unnecessary objects

rm(Input)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)


model = lmer(rank ~ species*treatment + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

summary(model)

> anova(model)
